# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
#sacu1 ^4kQG4nJZ

Def. (continuity at a): Let f: I -> R (interval I). a e I. f is continuous at a if limit f x->a is f(a). ^Hb66eZsc

Properties ^ybYYCsMy

Proposition (permanence of sign): if f continuous at a and f(a)>0. -> f(x)>0 for x close to a ^r2vRIVx2

[[Notes-DAncona-eng.pdf#page=88&annotation=1458R|Proof]] ^tMEaKZTr

    similar to def. of limit ^lTc3GxB7

Thm. (zeroes of continuous functions): If f continuous in interval [a, b] ^ f(a)>=0   f(b)<=0. -> E c e [a, b] f(c)=0 ^jlGtDNho

intuition: one cannot go from a + to - number w.o.
 crossing the x axis if function continuous ^c3Mb2tAI

Def. (continuity at I): Let f: I -> R (interval I). a e I. f is continuous at I if V a, lim x->a = f(a) ^k8F5VMS9

Thm. (Weistrass, Maximum and minimum): f continuous function 
defined in bounded closed interval [a, b]. E 2 points
 m ^ M s.t. m<=f(x)<=M (absolute max and absolute min) ^uTry5Ofm

Thm. (intermediate value): if f continuous function in [a,b], 
^ say m<=μ<=M. ⟶ E c e [a,b] where f(c)=μ ^gPrGfpR3

Proof: define function g(x)=f(x)-μ, ⟶ combine 
Weistrass thm. and zeroes thm. ^31qRtZOq
